### Round 1 | planner | planner_initial

- diagnosis: Task: infer the most likely AIE mechanism (ICT vs TICT vs ESIPT vs neutral-aromatic/RIM) for COc1ccc(/C(=C(/C#N)c2ccccc2)c2ccccc2)cc1.

Working top-1 hypothesis: TICT. Runner-up: ICT.

Why TICT is only a working hypothesis: the structure has a plausible donor–acceptor axis (anisole/aryl to cyano-substituted alkene) and multiple aryl rotors that can twist, which can yield a twisted charge-transfer state in solution; however, it may instead exhibit a more planar ICT state or primarily RIM-driven AIE like TPE analogs without a distinct TICT minimum.

Key uncertainty between TICT (top1) and ICT (top2): whether the lowest bright excited state is primarily charge-transfer and stabilized by significant twisting (TICT) versus remaining relatively conjugated/planar (ICT). Evidence that can separate them includes computed S1 character (charge-transfer metrics, dipole change), oscillator strength, and whether excited-state relaxation favors increased torsion around the exocyclic C=C/aryl bonds.

Context availability: a shared prepared structure is available and ready (41 atoms; 10 conformers generated; selected conformer id 2; 4 rotatable bonds; 3 aromatic rings).

Agent capabilities: Macro can provide structure-based and literature-analogy reasoning (e.g., TPE-like AIE/RIM vs D–A CT behavior) but cannot confirm excited-state character. Microscopic can run one bounded baseline S0/S1 computation on the prepared structure to provide vertical excitation energies, oscillator strengths, and qualitative CT indicators; it cannot (in round 1) perform conformer/torsion sensitivity or multi-step excited-state optimization.

Why gather both macro and microscopic evidence in round 1: Macro narrows plausible mechanisms using motif heuristics (triaryl-alkene + CN; rotor count; donor/acceptor balance), while the single baseline microscopic run provides the first quantitative check on whether low-lying excited states look CT-like (supporting ICT/TICT) or locally excited (supporting neutral-aromatic/RIM).

### Round 1 | macro | run_macro

- agent_name: macro

- status: success

- task_received: Assess macro-level structural evidence relevant to the current working hypothesis 'TICT'. Reuse the shared prepared structure context when available, summarize low-cost structural indicators only, and stay within current macro capability. Hypothesis uncertainty to keep in mind: Top1 (TICT) vs top2 (ICT) is uncertain because the molecule supports donor–acceptor conjugation but also resembles rotor-rich triaryl AIE scaffolds; a single vertical-excitation baseline can indicate CT propensity but may not capture a distinct twisted minimum without further geometry relaxation/torsion analysis.

- task_completion_status: contracted

- task_completion: Task was completed only in a capability-limited contracted form. The agent returned bounded macro evidence, but it could not complete unsupported parts of the Planner instruction: Computing/confirming a TICT minimum via excited-state geometry relaxation; Quantitative vertical-excitation CT metrics (oscillator strengths, NTOs, dipole changes); Aggregate-state/packing effects on restriction of intramolecular motion.

- task_understanding: Provide macro-level (low-cost, deterministic) structural evidence relevant to the working hypothesis TICT for the given molecule, prioritizing reuse of the shared prepared-structure context (topology + geometry proxies). Summarize indicators that would support or weaken a TICT interpretation versus a more planar ICT picture, without making a global mechanism adjudication or invoking unsupported simulations.

- reasoning_summary: From the shared structure context and SMILES, the molecule is a triaryl-alkene scaffold bearing a cyano substituent and a methoxy-substituted aryl ring (donor–acceptor motif embedded in a rotor-rich triaryl framework). Macro indicators consistent with potential TICT: (i) multiple aryl “rotors” and several torsion candidates (rotatable_bond_count=4; torsion_candidate_count=4) that can decouple donor/acceptor conjugation upon twisting; (ii) sterically congested triaryl/alkene core typical of twisted aryl–vinyl relationships, enabling twisted charge-transfer geometries in excited state even if the ground-state is more conjugated; (iii) donor–acceptor partition proxy is intermediate (0.5), suggesting some D–A separation rather than a purely locally excited aromatic system. Indicators leaning toward more ICT/planar conjugation (less distinct TICT): (i) planarity_proxy is high (~0.899), which is more consistent with a relatively conjugated/less-twisted baseline geometry; (ii) hetero count is low (2 total; effectively one donor OMe and one acceptor CN), so the acceptor strength and D–A contrast may be modest compared to classic strong push–pull TICT dyes; (iii) aromatic_ring_count=3 and ring_system_count=3 indicate three independent phenyls (not fused), which often remain twisted but can still support delocalized ICT without requiring a fully orthogonal TICT minimum. Overall, the structure has the right qualitative ingredients for TICT (D–A + torsional freedom), but the provided geometry proxy suggests the selected conformer is fairly planar, so structural evidence alone does not uniquely separate TICT from ICT without explicit torsion/dihedral readouts or excited-state relaxation (both out of scope here).
Capability limit note: This macro pass is limited to deterministic topology reading from SMILES and reuse of provided preparation proxies; it cannot compute actual dihedral angles from coordinates, scan torsions, or perform excited-state/vertical excitation calculations needed to conclusively distinguish TICT vs ICT.

- execution_plan: Use deterministic_macro_structure_scan to execute the bounded macro workflow with focus areas: Topology: donor (OMe aryl) vs acceptor (cyano) placement across conjugated vinyl/aryl system, Rotor richness: rotatable bonds and torsion candidates around aryl–vinyl connections, Geometry proxies: planarity_proxy, compactness_proxy, principal_span_proxy, conformer_dispersion_proxy as indirect CT/TICT plausibility cues. Planned local steps: [shared_context_load] Load the shared prepared structure context and reuse its descriptors. [focus_selection] Select the macro structural focus areas requested by the Planner instruction. [topology_analysis] Summarize rotor topology, ring systems, conjugation, and donor-acceptor layout. [geometry_proxy_analysis] Summarize planarity, torsion, compactness, and conformer-dispersion proxies.

- result_summary: The macro scan recorded aromatic_atom_count=18, hetero_atom_count=2, branch_point_count=6, rotatable_bond_count=4, planarity_proxy=0.898693, compactness_proxy=0.901811, and conformer_dispersion_proxy=1.0.
Key proxies: aromatic_atom_count=18, hetero_atom_count=2, branch_point_count=6, conjugation_proxy=5.899, flexibility_proxy=8.0, rotatable_bond_count=4, aromatic_ring_count=3, ring_system_count=3, donor_acceptor_partition_proxy=0.5, planarity_proxy=0.898693, compactness_proxy=0.901811, conformer_dispersion_proxy=1.0.

- remaining_local_uncertainty: Macro evidence alone cannot resolve excited-state relaxation behavior or external consistency; unresolved local gap: Macro evidence is limited to single-molecule low-cost structural and geometry proxies, so it still cannot resolve excited-state relaxation behavior, aggregation-state packing, or external consistency.

Macro indicators consistent with potential TICT: (i) multiple aryl “rotors” and several torsion candidates (rotatable_bond_count=4; torsion_candidate_count=4) that can decouple donor/acceptor conjugation upon twisting; (ii) sterically congested triaryl/alkene core typical of twisted aryl–vinyl relationships, enabling twisted charge-transfer geometries in excited state even if the ground-state is more conjugated; (iii) donor–acceptor partition proxy is intermediate (0.5), suggesting some D–A separation rather than a purely locally excited aromatic system. Indicators leaning toward more ICT/planar conjugation (less distinct TICT): (i) planarity_proxy is high (~0.899), which is more consistent with a relatively conjugated/less-twisted baseline geometry; (ii) hetero count is low (2 total; effectively one donor OMe and one acceptor CN), so the acceptor strength and D–A contrast may be modest compared to classic strong push–pull TICT dyes; (iii) aromatic_ring_count=3 and ring_system_count=3 indicate three independent phenyls (not fused), which often remain twisted but can still support delocalized ICT without requiring a fully orthogonal TICT minimum. Overall, the structure has the right qualitative ingredients for TICT (D–A + torsional freedom), but the provided geometry proxy suggests the selected conformer is fairly planar, so structural evidence alone does not uniquely separate TICT from ICT without explicit torsion/dihedral readouts or excited-state relaxation (both out of scope here).

- diagnosis: Round 3/20 (18 rounds remaining). Top1=ICT (0.37) vs Top2=neutral aromatic (0.31); TICT is now third (0.22).

Latest evidence: the targeted microscopic follow-up again failed to produce explicit CT descriptors (electron–hole separation/overlap, CT distance, NTO/donor–acceptor localization). What it did add is confirmation that the lowest two vertical states are both bright (S1 f≈0.2875 at 3.6776 eV; S2 f≈0.3353 at 4.5055 eV) and share the same primary virtual orbital, consistent with a relatively allowed, not-obviously-twisted vertical transition manifold. This slightly strengthens ICT relative to TICT (TICT often manifests as a relaxed, more twisted and frequently dimmer/darker state), but it also leaves neutral-aromatic/LE behavior viable because bright transitions are compatible with LE aromatic excitations.

Effect on hypotheses:
- ICT strengthened slightly (bright S1 + large S0 dipole still point to D–A polarization), but remains unconfirmed without CT localization metrics.
- Neutral aromatic strengthened as the main challenger because the internal workflow still cannot demonstrate CT character.
- TICT weakened relative to both ICT and neutral aromatic because no torsion-dependent signature or dark state is observed and the structure proxy remains fairly planar.

Key remaining discriminator (Top1 vs Top2): whether S1 is genuinely charge-transfer (donor→acceptor electron/hole separation or NTO localization onto OMe-ring vs CN region) versus mostly locally excited aromatic.

Capability limit note: run_targeted_state_characterization is bounded to fixed-geometry characterization on a small representative subset of an existing bundle and does not perform excited-state geometry relaxation or broad PES scans. If requested CT descriptors are not computable from the chosen low-cost method or available integrals, the action will report those descriptors as unavailable rather than attempt unsupported inference.
Failure policy: If one or more requested CT descriptors cannot be produced (e.g., unavailable integrals or unsupported low-cost method outputs), the run will:
1) Explicitly list each unavailable descriptor in the results.

3) Recommend (in the textual result) a minimal follow-up (reported as metadata only) if further observables are required — but the execution will not launch additional actions automatically.

### Round 5 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Round 5/20 (16 rounds remaining). Top1=ICT (0.50) vs Top2=neutral aromatic (0.25); additional candidate TICT (0.12).

Latest evidence impact: the microscopic `run_ris_state_characterization` execution again produced only proxy-level outputs (dominant transitions, state-family overlap, S0 dipole, Mulliken charges, MO files) and did NOT provide the requested CT/LE discriminators (attachment–detachment, difference densities, electron–hole centroids, or excited-state dipole change). It does, however, confirm (i) a large ground-state dipole (~8.17 D) and (ii) bright low-lying vertical excitations (S1 f≈0.37 at 3.75 eV; S2 f≈0.40 at 4.57 eV) with similar dominant transition signature (primarily 82→83; shared virtual orbital 83).

Effect on hypotheses:
- ICT: slightly weakened only in the sense that molecule-specific CT metrics remain unavailable internally; otherwise unchanged/slightly supported by large dipole and push–pull motif.
- Neutral aromatic: slightly strengthened relative to ICT because the internal pipeline still cannot demonstrate donor/acceptor-separated excitation for this exact molecule.
- TICT: unchanged to slightly weakened because repeated vertical results are bright and do not suggest a dominant dark twisted CT channel at the FC geometry.

Key remaining discriminator (ICT vs neutral aromatic): explicit orbital/transition localization (e.g., HOMO/HOMO-1 vs LUMO localization on OMe-aryl vs CN-aryl) or difference-density/NTO-style donor→acceptor separation; currently missing internally.

Verifier supplementation: sufficient (close-family + generic discriminators), but not molecule-specific.
Closure justification: still collecting and trending toward being blocked unless we can generate a molecule-specific localization surrogate.

Why next action: the most discriminative low-cost internal next step is to force orbital localization/fragment contributions for the orbitals participating in the dominant transition (81/82→83), which can directly separate donor→acceptor ICT-like character from a largely local aromatic excitation.

- action: microscopic

- confidence: 0.5

- task_instruction: Microscopic (single registry-backed action): run `run_targeted_localized_orbital_analysis` on artifact_bundle_id='round_01_baseline_bundle' (or reuse the most recent fixed-geometry follow-up artifacts if the action supports it) to localize and quantify the key orbitals involved in the bright transition(s): occupied orbitals 81 and 82 and virtual orbital 83 (and, if produced automatically, 84–85). Required deliverables: (1) localized-orbital (e.g., Pipek–Mezey) population/fragment contribution summary for these orbitals; (2) a short mapping of whether the hole-side orbitals (81/82) are primarily on the methoxy-aryl vs other phenyls and whether the electron-side orbital (83) is primarily on the cyano-bearing region. Goal: provide a molecule-specific ICT-vs-LE surrogate via donor/acceptor orbital separation. Do not attempt excited-state relaxation.

The latest RIS run confirms bright low-lying excitations and large S0 dipole but cannot, by itself, decide whether the excitation is donor→acceptor CT-like or largely local aromatic.

- final_hypothesis_rationale: null

- capability_assessment: Macro is adequate for motif/topology (push–pull + rotor count + planarity proxy) but cannot deliver excited-state character.
